Judge and Mrs. Brsklne Mayo Bos*
of Los Angeles were house guests at *
delightful week's end party given by
the Misses Morrison at their San Jose
home.
Last Saturday the hostesses enter
tained at a dinner of eighteen covers,
the decorations being of lovely design-
Over the round table was a canopy ot
smilax, while all about the cloth were
scattered i^ridesaaald roses and maiden
hair f>rn great bowls of Ameri
can Beauty roses, the place cards beam
ing roses In- water color. D Â°
A luncheon and tea occupied the
greater part of Sunday afternoon, sev

COLLINS SEEKS
FURTHER DELAY
Accused' Attorney Is Grasp
. ing .â¢ Desperately' at ..All-
Possible " . Technicalities
' With the desperation of a drowning
man clutching at* straws, George- D. Col
lins_ is -grasping at every available tech
nicality. 'Because^ .of the length of the
Uriburu case Judge Lennon was unable

yesterday, and it was continued till 10
o'clock to-day for the defendant to plead.
Collins gave notice that he would then
move to quash the indictment for perjury,
and failing to gain that point would move
to set it aside.
This* proceeding -will necessitate lengthy
arguments and enable Collins to gain fur
ther delay. The accused attorney was in
excellent spirits yesterday and wore the
expression bf.a man who could see noth
ing ahead But a' winning fight.
In. his counter "affidavit Collins has al
ready given an inkling of the grounds he.
will Bet forth In support of his motion to'
set aside or quash the indictment. He
.has already alleged that the perjury in
dictment was made solely for the purpose
of having him brought back from Canada.
He will probably. -attack the validity of
the jury, as he has done before.
Judge Lennon tried to" ascertain 'from
the evasive attorney how^ long it. would
take tQ present the law points of these
motions. Collins did . not r-know. V Judge
Lennon figured that half an hour would
be ample time. Collins has applied for a
writ of "prohibition from the "Supreme
Court to, prevent Judge Lennon from,sit
ting in the case on the grounds of preju
d.ice and bias. All the witnesses in the
case are/ ordered to appear to-day. :

.irthe Lena had not been steaming at

posed' to be up-to-date. The exhibition

parture Is neither the first nor worst
offense.
When the Lena,\ outward-bound,
reached a point abreast of Alcatraz the
flag was hoisted- and a national salute
fired from the Lena's battery. U The sa
lute was fired "shipshape and Â» Bristol
fashion," twenty-one guns, with five
second .intervals * between each j explo
sion. As the echo of the last gun died
away Old Glory was hauled down and
stored aw,ay in the Lena's signal locker.
The Lena was making slow headway,
but with all her lingering was almost
at Fort Point' before* a gun, boomed
from Alcatraz. * Between some of the
shots fired from the army saluting sta
tion there. were intervals of from five
to* ten minutes; and the Lena was al
most at sea before her, salute had been
returned in full. â
When the "Italian cruiser Calabria ar
rived here not long ago she fired a na
tional salute as S she passed 'Alcatraz.

traz ba.ttery responded. ' â¢
